  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_58732af4-46ca-4604-9bdb-67a521fdfd32'
      });

  <span id="freeText44142645627086142" style="display:none">As the NSA gets a strong lead on one of the most prominent faces of ISIS, the Islamic State embarks on a bold course of action-an attack on American soil. Former Navy SEAL Adam Taylor, on a break between assignments for a global paramilitary security firm, is visiting his folks in his home town when he gets a new mission-provide security for a rock star who is in town for a St. Patrick's Day concert. Unknown to Adam, a team of American ISIS soldiers will soon arrive with a plan to wreak havoc on the Jersey Shore, and Adam will get caught up in a deadly game of wits between the terrorist menace and those tasked to protect the citizens of the homeland.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2104892395" />
    <a title="Sandy S" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6441069-sandy-s"><img alt="Sandy S" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320628496p2/6441069.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2104892395?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy S" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy S" href="/user/show/6441069-sandy-s">Sandy S</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2104892395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11603719162074380395">4.25 stars<br/><br/>ABOUT THE BOOK: Release Date November 2016<br/><br/>As the NSA gets a strong lead on one of the most prominent faces of ISIS, the Islamic State embarks on a bold course of action-an attack on American soil. Former Navy SEAL Adam Taylor, on a break between assignments for a global paramilitary security firm, is visiting his folks in his home town when he gets a new mission-provide security for a rock star who is in town for a St. Patrick's Day concert. Unknown to Adam, a team of American ISIS sol</span>
  <span id="freeText11603719162074380395" style="display:none">4.25 stars<br /><br />ABOUT THE BOOK: Release Date November 2016<br /><br />As the NSA gets a strong lead on one of the most prominent faces of ISIS, the Islamic State embarks on a bold course of action-an attack on American soil. Former Navy SEAL Adam Taylor, on a break between assignments for a global paramilitary security firm, is visiting his folks in his home town when he gets a new mission-provide security for a rock star who is in town for a St. Patrick's Day concert. Unknown to Adam, a team of American ISIS soldiers will soon arrive with a plan to wreak havoc on the Jersey Shore, and Adam will get caught up in a deadly game of wits between the terrorist menace and those tasked to protect the citizens of the homeland.<br /><br />••••••••••••••••<br /><br />REVIEW: Told from several third person perspectives WHEN THE REAPER COMES by John L. DeBoer is an action packed, suspense thriller focusing on home grown terrorism, ISIS supporters, and the ensuing operation that will see several government agencies outwit and outsmart a planned attack against American rock idol Brian Callahan whose anti-Muslim comments have caught the attention of the Islamic State. Enter former Navy SEAL and GSG (Global Security Guardian) specialist Adam Taylor whose latest assignment to protect Brian becomes complicated when three known ISIS sympathizers target Adam’s charge in a planned terrorist plot to take down as many people at the rock star’s concert. What ensues is the search for the people responsible as Adam and several security agencies of the US government coordinate a well-organized plan of attack.<br /><br />WHEN THE REAPER COMES is a story of good vs evil; of intrigue, mystery, action and suspense. John L. DeBoer weaves an infinitely detailed story line of fanaticism, religious faith, retaliation against American citizens, and the growing threat by ISIS-the Jihadist militant group that targets anyone and anything that stands in direct opposition to the Islamic State. There is a large ensemble cast of secondary and supporting characters including several members of the FBI and NSA, local and state police forces, US Marshalls, independent and private government security, ISIS militants, powerful financial Middle East politicians, and an assortment of former Vietnam Veterans itching to take down anyone targeting American citizens.<br /><br />From Iraq to New Jersey WHEN THE REAPER COMES gets up close and personal with a terrorist organization that is determined to destroy the American faith. The world has grown increasingly smaller when American citizens become targets of some of their own. The premise is engaging, intense and suspenseful; the action is thrilling and imaginative. My only concerns are the actions and intentions of one of the NSA agents-in reality the agent’s motives and behavior would have been flagged, investigated and not easily ignored in the face of ISIS and Islamic threats against the Western nations. I question the believability and our hero’s major lack of entanglement as to the potential threats against everyone concerned. At the very least, the agent’s connections are a big cause for alarm.<br /><br />Copy supplied for review<br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2985502508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2985502508" />
    <a title="Mrs. Y" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83393925-mrs-y"><img alt="Mrs. Y" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532384638p2/83393925.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2985502508?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mrs. Y" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mrs. Y" href="/user/show/83393925-mrs-y">Mrs. Y</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32993527-when-the-reaper-comes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83393925-mrs-y?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83393925-mrs-y?shelf=crime-review">crime-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2985502508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8017307835174199971">There are some things in my childhood that I always loved, and one of those things was the classic adventure summer blockbuster film. These specific films were trendy in the 1990s and frequently had very distinct character arcs, portrayal in the culture, and ideas of good versus evil. <br/><br/>In today's review, I am reviewing the novel by John L. DeBoer, "When the Reaper Comes." John was kind enough to ask me to give an honest review, and I picked this up on Kindle Unlimited. <br/><br/>Starting with my first impr</span>
  <span id="freeText8017307835174199971" style="display:none">There are some things in my childhood that I always loved, and one of those things was the classic adventure summer blockbuster film. These specific films were trendy in the 1990s and frequently had very distinct character arcs, portrayal in the culture, and ideas of good versus evil. <br /><br />In today's review, I am reviewing the novel by John L. DeBoer, "When the Reaper Comes." John was kind enough to ask me to give an honest review, and I picked this up on Kindle Unlimited. <br /><br />Starting with my first impressions, As a reader, my imagination traveled to a simple story, rooted in the political climate around 2012 - 2016. There are distinct good guys, and definite bad guys and the initial premise and hook were easy to get into and understand. Thus, for my first impression, I found this novel to be comforting in its use of familiar tropes and exciting in how it used them. <br /><br />I don't want to spoil this novel, so I am not going to. I can say that I found the most consistent element to the story was how clearly defined the character arcs are. There were no characters who blurred or met a gray line in the morality or ethics of their side. This unique take is something that I haven't read in more recently published novels. I found myself as a reader reassured by the fact that my expectations were never subverted, and there was no major twist nor any story trick.<br /><br />So let me go into my critiques now, and under "Cliche' Much," unfortunately, there are a couple of hits. Villains are villains, I told you this already, but the ones in this novel are such a stereotypical villain character type, that they are bumbling and one dimensional. The leader has a strong personality, is stubborn despite himself, and has an excellent character arch. The 'muscle' characters become typical for secondary villain characters, mostly following because they must for the plot to work. And that's not bad exactly, but it is a critique, and I did notice it. The same tropes exist for "The good guys are good guys" because, honestly, they were the same. In my opinion, should someone change the politics and setting, the characters could fit comfortably in any novel. One could replace either side with any number of scenarios, aside from the specifics to the political piece. While there were some unique pieces to each character, I found was those pieces didn't matter. The characters were used in such bold strokes through the narrative the uniqueness was lost. <br /><br />Let me go into what I enjoyed about "When the Reaper Comes," we are going to start with the "Story Structure, Foundation, and presentation" category. I think this is the first time that I have ever said all three of these items were done well and in harmony. The novel was easy to read on Kindle with the default settings. The Kindle also was graced with well-spaced margins. I am happy to report that there were no spelling or grammatical errors. In "Story Structure" the layout of the novel was done plot by plot, it had marked character arcs, and you could set your watch on "this event will happen at 25%, and this one at 50%" like clockwork. I wasn't ever given any boring, dry parts to pacing, the tension was just right for the scene, and I found it to be exciting. Lastly, under "Foundation," I found all of the science, tech, information on weapons, and any technical parts of the story, including political reasons, were outlined well. There wasn't anything confusing in presentation, and I found this book to be simplistic in its complicated nature. <br /><br />I've yet to meet a book that fits all three categories so well, so I think that John did a fantastic job in writing "When the Reaper Comes." If he has an editor or story editing team, they deserve a bottle of fine wine for all of their efforts, because they did so well at making sure all reader needs were met. <br /><br />Next, under the category "Whole Story," I am pleased to say this story has a complete story. There were no subversions of expectations, no unnecessary cliffhangers, no lost plot-threads, and it was fully fleshed out. As a reader, I appreciated the backstories to every character, and I felt the weight of the choices both sides of the antagonist as well as the protagonist faced. Again, John did an exceptional job with writing this story and making sure that all things came to a satisfactory conclusion.<br /><br />In my last thoughts, while I don't think I'm the intended audience of this novel, I can assure you that if you are, you should be fully satisfied with this book. If you like James Bond Spy novels or you love Jason Borne, or perhaps you are a big fan of books that mirror the "Die Hard" movies, this book is for you. "When the Reaper Comes" is an action-packed fuel-driven fun fest, and I hope you enjoy every moment of it. <br /><br /><br />Score<br />And thus, "When The Reaper Comes" gets a score of 90/100, which is a five-star review on Goodreads and Amazon. Again, if you are interested in a popcorn-munching good time where bad guys are villains, and good guys are heroes, pick this book up! You will not be disappointed! </span>
  <a data-text-id="8017307835174199971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13132162492957576492">Title – When The Reaper Comes<br/>Author – John DeBoer<br/>Genre – M, S, T <br/>295 Amazon Pages<br/>Rating	4 stars out of 5		Posted 3/22/17<br/>15 - 2017<br/><br/>My impressions: Frightening, religious fanatics, well written & edited, strong characters, vigilante justice.<br/><br/>Main Characters:<br/>Cliff Evans – decapitated by American Radical Muslim terrorist who is then sent back to the USA.<br/>Adam Taylor – age 38 ex-Navy Seal, working for Global Security Guardian.<br/>Mario Martinez – age 37, Adam’s friend and partner.<br/>Peter Crandall - NSA analys</span>
  <span id="freeText13132162492957576492" style="display:none">Title – When The Reaper Comes<br />Author – John DeBoer<br />Genre – M, S, T <br />295 Amazon Pages<br />Rating	4 stars out of 5		Posted 3/22/17<br />15 - 2017<br /><br />My impressions: Frightening, religious fanatics, well written &amp; edited, strong characters, vigilante justice.<br /><br />Main Characters:<br />Cliff Evans – decapitated by American Radical Muslim terrorist who is then sent back to the USA.<br />Adam Taylor – age 38 ex-Navy Seal, working for Global Security Guardian.<br />Mario Martinez – age 37, Adam’s friend and partner.<br />Peter Crandall - NSA analyst.<br />Amira Bahar – Lebanese, NSA analyst.<br />Angela Martin – Participant in terrorist plot until she had second thoughts.<br />Yusuf Khouri – American born Radical Muslim terrorist. <br />Brian Callahan – Rock Musician who publicly offended the Islamic religion and is targeted by ISIS terrorist.<br /><br />The story begins in Erbil Iraq as Adam and Mario provide security for CNN reporter Maxwell Rice. There are enlightening scenes of the security detail before Adam and Mario return to the US on vacation. While at home Adam and a friend pick up two women in a bar. He is attracted to Angela and wants to date her again. She confesses to him that she is involved in a terrorist plot to take place in his hometown of Spring Lake, New Jersey and regrets agreeing to participate.<br />From there the plot picks up speed and has more twist and turns than a winding mountain road. The good guys and the bad guys keep revising their plans to react to the opposition. The terrorist spot Adam and learn his identity. With that information, they target his parents’ home to punish him for trying to abort their plans.<br />As expected there is a united effort between the local police and sheriff’s departments, the state police, FBI and U.S. Marshalls. And still the terrorists elude them until the very end. Adam then ensured the terrorist leader wouldn’t escape punishment.<br />I enjoyed this fast-paced story and recommend it. My negative impression is that the ending seemed a little weak concerning Amira’s actions and her future.<br /><br />The editing and sentence structure are excellent. Character development is thorough and compelling.<br />The plot is standard good guys vs. the evil terrorist but is presented well.<br /><br />This review was provided in exchange for a free book.<br />Vigilant Reader Book Reviews.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14687771372683995067">John DeBoer's 8th novel, When the Reaper Comes, truly fits into his international thriller award status. This thriller is fast-paced consistently eliciting moods of anticipation, suspense, and surprise. There is lots to know--ideas and real world information to pull together as narrative develops. The CIA, FBI, NSA, ISIS, NSA, SEALs, and more, interconnect with a diverse collection of characters and settings.<br/><br/>The shifting locations even included Canada, and Long Branch, Ontario (even closer to ho</span>
  <span id="freeText14687771372683995067" style="display:none">John DeBoer's 8th novel, When the Reaper Comes, truly fits into his international thriller award status. This thriller is fast-paced consistently eliciting moods of anticipation, suspense, and surprise. There is lots to know--ideas and real world information to pull together as narrative develops. The CIA, FBI, NSA, ISIS, NSA, SEALs, and more, interconnect with a diverse collection of characters and settings.<br /><br />The shifting locations even included Canada, and Long Branch, Ontario (even closer to home). The politics around border crossings changes constantly in real life as well. I couldn't help but think of how the situation in the book is juxtaposed to our current border crossing focus. In deed, DeBoer's eclectic settings reach the interests of a wide-reading audience.<br /><br />When the novel opens, I was instantly compelled to continue to read as the Reaper comes to take Cliff from the dank dungeon he shared with other imprisoned journalists. No Reaper ever brought good news but did Cliff sense something different in this normally dooming situation? <br /><br />Cliffhangers gallore--When the Reaper Comes keeps us on our toes! It's a great book, a must read! And, importantly, we have strong female characters including Barbara Pliskin as director of FBI's Counterterrorism--what's not to love:)<br /><br />More reading lists, author and book talks at the Art Matrix, Writer Share Cafe!<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://artmatrix.ca/books">https://artmatrix.ca/books</a></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A.B. Funkhauser" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A.B. Funkhauser" href="/user/show/41622637-a-b-funkhauser">A.B. Funkhauser</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2356890808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12803498662864223244">TERROR IN JERSEY<br/><br/>There’s something very cool about author John DeBoer’s latest outing. Moving beyond mystery he explores ideological warfare—in this case, home grown terrorism—with an eye to the family unit. Ex-Navy SEAL Adam Taylor works for a security contractor with anchors in some of the world’s most dangerous places. Averting kidnaps, torture and death for radical agendas are part of his job description. His tasks are far from rote, but when an ISIS executioner plots a Boston-style bombing i</span>
  <span id="freeText12803498662864223244" style="display:none">TERROR IN JERSEY<br /><br />There’s something very cool about author John DeBoer’s latest outing. Moving beyond mystery he explores ideological warfare—in this case, home grown terrorism—with an eye to the family unit. Ex-Navy SEAL Adam Taylor works for a security contractor with anchors in some of the world’s most dangerous places. Averting kidnaps, torture and death for radical agendas are part of his job description. His tasks are far from rote, but when an ISIS executioner plots a Boston-style bombing in Taylor’s own backyard, his investment increases a thousandfold. Friends, colleagues, neighbors and even his shotgun-toting mom will join forces to protect their home. And this is what makes the story unique. Taylor’s family, home, town, city and country form a seamless unit that serves as a grand metaphor to Taylor’s self and psyche: Who are you and what are you willing to do to safeguard your soul is the overarching question and we read on to find out just that. Taylor is backed by a huge cast that includes FBI, CIA, NSA, the local constabulary and regular folks he grew up with. I enjoyed When the Reaper Comes not just for its colorful villains and matchless heroes, but for the detail DeBoer lends to his narrative. From the nuts and bolts planning behind a counter terrorist op to the military ordnance required to deliver results fascinated from beginning to end. 5 Stars for a good time and a super ending.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12803498662864223244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike Siedschlag" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike Siedschlag" href="/user/show/31817086-mike-siedschlag">Mike Siedschlag</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1945378369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1451229689902172355">Disclaimer: You know it; don't make me type it out.<br/><br/>When the Reaper Comes, authored by John L. DeBoer, is an exciting action/suspense/thriller pitting American security experts against American born terrorists. <br/><br/>The bad guys (that would be the terrorists) want to make a statement while killing a popular musician who said things about terrorists that they didn't like. The good guys are the security agents assigned to protect the musician.<br/><br/>A lot of supporting characters (on both sides) come together </span>
  <span id="freeText1451229689902172355" style="display:none">Disclaimer: You know it; don't make me type it out.<br /><br />When the Reaper Comes, authored by John L. DeBoer, is an exciting action/suspense/thriller pitting American security experts against American born terrorists. <br /><br />The bad guys (that would be the terrorists) want to make a statement while killing a popular musician who said things about terrorists that they didn't like. The good guys are the security agents assigned to protect the musician.<br /><br />A lot of supporting characters (on both sides) come together in a compelling chess game. Advantage shifts between players continuously, each trying to guess their opponents next move. Both sides are smart so the story shifts back and forth keeping the reader hooked. Like a chess game, targets come and go with the flow of events. Twists, turns, surprises, and questionable alliances abound. <br /><br />The positive and negative in this story is the same; It is an extremely plausible plot. As the reader, I never said to myself, "that could never happen". The scary thing is that it really could happen, and there are so many variables which could lead to many different outcomes. <br /><br />Violence (hello, terrorists), suspense, intrigue, and a bit of romance keeps this a taut, spellbinding, and eminently entertaining read. <br /><br />When the Reaper Comes, by John L. DeBoer is a scary story that could be actually happening as you read it. I'll admit it scared me in a way that I'm not used to. If you like your thrills and chills on the more plausible and realistic side, When the Reaper Comes will get your blood pumping. Enjoy!<br /><br />Mike</span>
  <a data-text-id="1451229689902172355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Oh My Bookness" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5891236-oh-my-bookness"><img alt="Oh My Bookness" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329377127p2/5891236.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2007891269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7641793854766138200">When The Reaper Comes by John DeBoer, is a fitting name to call one of the terrorist group that seems to fester through our homeland murdering innocent people.<br/><br/> Adam is bodyguarding a musician who pissed off ISIS and now is coming full frontal on him which is located in Adams home town. This novel tells the story of Adam, a ex-navy seal, and his partner. They have to stay ahead and strong in the game,  there are many struggles ahead. There's also many style characters that attribute to either sid</span>
  <span id="freeText7641793854766138200" style="display:none">When The Reaper Comes by John DeBoer, is a fitting name to call one of the terrorist group that seems to fester through our homeland murdering innocent people.<br /><br /> Adam is bodyguarding a musician who pissed off ISIS and now is coming full frontal on him which is located in Adams home town. This novel tells the story of Adam, a ex-navy seal, and his partner. They have to stay ahead and strong in the game,  there are many struggles ahead. There's also many style characters that attribute to either sides of the fight. Adam recruits friends that have experience in securing defens. <br /><br />The book is full of twists and turns that'll keep you guessing. Asking yourselves, what's next? Our heroes find themselves in the most complicated conditions and choices to make, but will they make them wisely? You'll have to read it to find out.<br /><br /> This is a novel that will make you stop and think what's going on in the real world with ISIS. The situation in this novel could maybe come true, you never know. Reading the newspapers and watching the television about all the crazies out there on our home soil that actually join ISIS, anything is possible. <br /><br /><br /> I enjoyed this novel and had a hard time putting it down, if you like thrills, chill and action that'll keep you up wanting for more then I recommend this novel.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14068848947451553288">With terrorism being such a terrifying but also fascinating concept, and is executed very well in this novel by John L. DeBoer. I have to say even though I hadn’t heard of DeBoer previously, When the Reaper Comes did not fail to deliver.<br/><br/>The writing is pacey and punchy, much as you’d expect in an action thriller, and the plot has enough twists and surprises to keep you in that ‘</span>
  <span id="freeText14068848947451553288" style="display:none">With terrorism being such a terrifying but also fascinating concept, and is executed very well in this novel by John L. DeBoer. This was a book recommended by a friend of mine who knows I’ve enjoyed books by authors such as Tom Clancy is the past. I have to say even though I hadn’t heard of DeBoer previously, When the Reaper Comes did not fail to deliver.<br /><br />The writing is pacey and punchy, much as you’d expect in an action thriller, and the plot has enough twists and surprises to keep you in that ‘just one more page’ mindset, so that I slept in for work one day after reading too late the night before. I suppose that in itself is a ringing endorsement, so make sure you allow enough time before embarking on this page-turner yourself.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1818022801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1818022801" />
    <a title="Stanley McShane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18437927-stanley-mcshane"><img alt="Stanley McShane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494544464p2/18437927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1818022801?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stanley McShane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stanley McShane" href="/user/show/18437927-stanley-mcshane">Stanley McShane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1818022801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15881775063004357141"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32898313.When_the_Reaper_Comes' title='When the Reaper Comes by John L Deboer' rel='nofollow noopener'>When the Reaper Comes</a> Like watching it play out on the big screen in full Technicolor and Dolby, the action from the beginning of "When the Reaper Comes" by John DeBoer was so well laid out, it was difficult to hit the pause button until the last scene played out. I do enjoy a good thriller and have read my share of both military and political themed novels, including stories that include the present day battle with ISIS. So much of the philosophy zooms over our heads and is usually far enough r</span>
  <span id="freeText15881775063004357141" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32898313.When_the_Reaper_Comes" title="When the Reaper Comes by John L Deboer" rel="nofollow noopener">When the Reaper Comes</a> Like watching it play out on the big screen in full Technicolor and Dolby, the action from the beginning of "When the Reaper Comes" by John DeBoer was so well laid out, it was difficult to hit the pause button until the last scene played out. I do enjoy a good thriller and have read my share of both military and political themed novels, including stories that include the present day battle with ISIS. So much of the philosophy zooms over our heads and is usually far enough removed off our own soil that it is fairly easy to stick our heads in the sand and try to pretend it isn't happening. Unfortunately, it is, and America is no longer the isolated and protected country it once was. The concept of being infiltrated from within isn't a new one. Our protagonist is a former Navy SEAL, Adam Taylor, who, along with his partner receives a temporary assignment in Adam's hometown in upstate eastern US. The two are to help protect a rock star giving a concert who has made some dangerous and inflammatory errors concerning the Islamic State. As with any good cinema, the reader can be the proverbial fly on the wall in the terrorists' group planning sessions, as well as the NSA members responsible for the discovery and execution of their own plan for capture and custody of the antagonists. Adam also enlists the aid of boyhood friends; now law enforcement. As the intrigue develops and Adam is able to keep one step ahead of Khouri, the plot moves faster and faster. Can he continue to outwit the men with the IED, weapons, and plan for escape? The dialogue runs so real, you could almost join the conversation. I was given a copy of this book in exchange for a review, and I must say it was a very good bargain! Recommended for any thriller fans as well as those looking for a very topical revelation of the current conflict. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4107476.John_L__DeBoer" title="John L. DeBoer" rel="nofollow noopener">John L. DeBoer</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15881775063004357141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1874509600" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1874509600" />
    <a title="Maia Gomez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57035381-maia-gomez"><img alt="Maia Gomez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599066527p2/57035381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1874509600?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maia Gomez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maia Gomez" href="/user/show/57035381-maia-gomez">Maia Gomez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874509600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5694777595827664210">Wow- this was one fast-paced and intense read that is actually almost terrifying since it's something that can actually happen any day now! The book stayed at a really steady pace and was full of action, twists and complex situations that really had me sitting on the edge of my seat the whole time! I loved how you get to see several different characters points of view at the same time, giving you every side of the story, which makes it all the more intense. The way the author executed everything</span>
  <span id="freeText5694777595827664210" style="display:none">Wow- this was one fast-paced and intense read that is actually almost terrifying since it's something that can actually happen any day now! The book stayed at a really steady pace and was full of action, twists and complex situations that really had me sitting on the edge of my seat the whole time! I loved how you get to see several different characters points of view at the same time, giving you every side of the story, which makes it all the more intense. The way the author executed everything to coordinate together was just masterful! You get to see things with Adam, an ex SEAL and current bodyguard for a patriotic rockstar as he tries to outhink the terrorists and figure out where they're most likely to strike next. You also get special insight with Amira, a NSA intelligence operator who thinks she's on a peaceful weekend getaway but instead ends up smack dab in the middle of conspiracy. Also, you get to be part of the terrorists point of view as they race around trying to make a strike, yet keep getting thwarted by Adam and his team. <br />I found this book wildly entertaining, yet very intense and suspenseful, keeping my mind racing to keep up with everything. Even though I'm not too huge on military and war type books, I thoroughly enjoyed every minute of this one and highly suggest it to anybody that wants a really good thrill! I think it's almost scary that something like this really could be happening right this second somewhere.....</span>
  <a data-text-id="5694777595827664210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cbkUBcc47XfcsVnAU0B89PbZHBQTkGAp65ATV6eNIMnT+mRP+k7KGXy+TX3o+FkrMMDYddrGdxaafDAgTD8qEQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('haq6f8AEPg+eaKYtDc79XoGUoOKRFZWeiCjP4IyxasEn6co1/XIZYT5nspC2dtiBR41kg1hDgqH5xOyXZwNgGQ==')})
  }

The entire collection, in aggregate, is novel length. But unlike a novel, the reader can enjoy the stories over a period of time, even reading o<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText4677561057072377910\" style=\"display:none\">City Lights &amp; Side Streets is an assemblage of four short stories, a novelette, and a Salem Reid novella. The entire collection, in aggregate, is novel length. But unlike a novel, the reader can enjoy the stories over a period of time, even reading other works between each tale if desired.\nThe first short in the collection, The Crease in the Duvet, is written from the female perspective. A suburban mother deals with the angst of living with a husband whom she both loves and resents, vacillating between the two emotions several times in the course of a day…until tragedy strikes! \nNext, Clarence takes us back to the eighties. After getting high in the park, a couple of teenage brothers decide it’s a fine idea to allow an odd and possibly mentally unstable young man they know from the neighborhood to tag along to their niece’s birthday party. Needless to say, he’s not welcomed with open arms. A stunning turn of events occurs during the celebration and during the weeks that follow.\nLab Rat, a Salem Reid novella, anchors the collection. Unlike the gritty characters in the trilogy of novels previously published, Salem Reid tackles an occurrence of white-collar crime and corporate espionage within an analytical laboratory of a fertility drug maker.\nFollowing Lab Rat, The Scheduler is a lighthearted and humorous tale of a family of four and how their hectic lifestyles lead them to hire an organizer to keep everything straight…until it all backfires! \nThe last of the shorts is Dad Gab, another tale written from the female perspective. The story is about a young woman coming to terms with the loss of her father. As the girl stands on a pier above the ocean preparing to send Dad’s ashes to sea, she reminisces about the walks and talks she enjoyed with her father during her high school years.\nThe collection concludes with a novelette that may be the feminine version of Brown’s literary fiction piece, The Gravel Road. A young female bartender forms an unlikely bond with a sophisticated dying woman, and the two share deep secrets with each other as they navigate their unique relationship. The Sand Dune is a tale of marginal individuals with whom we gradually sympathize as we discover the pain and misfortune they all have endured.\nCity Lights &amp; Side Streets is the perfect reading companion for the busy bookworm, as small chunks of the collection can be read at irregular intervals without losing the continuity the reader might surrender in a full-length novel!<\/span>\n  <a <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer218365035329384212">After graduating from the University of Vermont College of Medicine, John L. DeBoer, M.D., F.A.C.S. completed his surgical training in the U.S. Army and then spent three years in the Medical Corps as a general surgeon. Thirty years of private practice later, he retired to begin a new career as a writer.<br/><br/>The father of two grown sons, he lives with his wife in North Carolina.</span>
